Second Day of the National Convention of the Women's Temperance Association

The China Women's Temperance Association held the second day of its national convention yesterday. Meetings were held starting at 8:00 am, and resolutions were passed on many important cases in the national women's community. At 8:00 am, a spiritual ceremony was held. The meeting began at 9:00 am, chaired by Ms. Chen Yueyun, followed by a lecture by Ms. Li Guanfang on "The Necessity of Transforming Chinese Families." There was a break from 10:00 am to 10:15 am. Discussions began at 11:15 am. The meeting continued from 2:00 pm, chaired by Mrs. Zheng Wei, with lectures by Ms. Zheng Yuzhi and Ms. Shi Yunmei on "The Vocational Problems of Chinese Women." Discussions followed. From 7:00 pm to 8:00 pm, Mrs. Han Zhang Wangzhen and Luo Longji gave a lecture on "The Legal Status of Women." From 8:00 pm to 9:00 pm, further discussions were held on various important cases, and the meeting adjourned. (1) Resolutions on important cases: Regarding the organization of the general association, (A) Regarding the association's district work, five districts were divided in East, West, South, and North China, and each district was assigned a traveling director to be responsible for handling matters. (B) In addition to the association's board of directors and secretariat, local youth group temperance troops and white knot teams are all affiliated with the branch associations. (C) The scope of relief should be expanded to beggars, maids, and disabled women and children. (D) The anti-drug movement must encompass opium, cigarettes, alcohol, and addictive narcotics. (E) Publication of periodicals should be expanded. (F) Promote proper family entertainment to eliminate gambling and other bad habits. (2) Regarding local branch associations, (A) In addition to engaging in social services, a membership solicitation meeting should be held every year. (B) Speech competition. (C) Children's recreation meeting. (D) White knot ceremony. All of the above cases were passed by a three-vote majority. Discussion of various cases, followed by discussion of women's movement matters: (1) Regarding women's status in the family (Li Guanfang, the chief writer of Duobao, lectured on the necessity of family transformation). (2) The most suitable marriage for China. (3) Marital relationship (A) Which is more harmful, divorce or concubinage? (B) How to maintain a long-term harmonious relationship between husband and wife? (2) How to promote children's happiness. Regarding women's vocational aspects (Jiang Wenyu, the director-general, lectured first, followed by a discussion. (A) How to cultivate specialized talents for women? (B) How to make women have a spirit of service? (C) Should married women have full-day work? (D) How to improve the lives of female workers and promote the government to implement factory laws?

Negotiation on Unauthorized Carriage of Foreigners by Ferry

A few days ago, the Passport Inspection Office of the Second Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau received a telegram from the Wusong Office stating that the Asiamar Oil Company's Si Mai (transliteration) steamer had arrived in Wusong today. Deputy Director Chen Timin went to the scene with inspectors Zhou Chunyue and others, and together with customs and quarantine officers, took a small boat to inspect the Si Mai steamer. However, upon arrival, they saw a lighter alongside the steamer and luggage being unloaded from the large steamer onto the lighter. At that time, the Si Mai large steamer was flying a yellow flag. According to regulations, a yellow flag indicates that quarantine has not yet been carried out, and passengers on the steamer are not allowed to disembark. Director Chen believed that the small boat had violated regulations by taking passengers and luggage without waiting for quarantine and passport inspection, so he went to inspect the small boat. He found one passenger and more than ten pieces of luggage in the cabin. The passenger was from Norway and had come to China on the Si Mai. Although he had a passport, it had not been endorsed by the Chinese embassy abroad. He was ordered to fill out a registration form, declare three pieces of luggage, and go to the Public Security Bureau for endorsement. It was then learned that the violating small boat was a boat of the British-owned Wusong Ferry Company that was picking up pilots and passengers. He was questioned why the company had violated regulations and disrupted work, undermining friendly relations, as the Municipal Public Security Bureau had notified the consulates of various countries in Shanghai, through the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' note to the ministers of various countries and the letter from the Municipal Government and the Public Security Bureau, that passengers were not allowed to disembark until the passports of foreign ships entering the country had been inspected. If a passenger without a passport or a wanted criminal was smuggled into the country, who would be responsible? Since this was the responsibility of his position, it was difficult to forgive. The violating ferry was detained. Subsequently, someone came forward to mediate, claiming that the passengers on the ferry were not passengers but pilots. However, according to the passenger's own registration form, he came to China from Norway and brought three pieces of luggage. The evidence was conclusive and there was no room for denial. It is reported that the matter has been reported to the Public Security Bureau, and the Municipal Government has been requested to seriously negotiate with the consulate in charge and punish them.

Black-Clad Thieves at Zhuhang Wharf

Suddenly Came Three People

Robbed Large and Small Silver Dollars

Yuan Weiting, a local, 38 years old, operates a Ruifeng Cigarette and Paper Store at No. 606 in Zhuhang Wharf, Nanshi. Around 7:00 pm the night before last, three robbers suddenly came. Electric Car Kills Xing Afu

Xing Afu, a resident of Jiangbei, was eighty-four years old. He lived at 332 Broadway Road. Yesterday afternoon at 4:20 PM, he went to buy snacks nearby and was crossing the road. At that time, a tram numbered 176 was speeding along. Xing was unable to avoid it and was knocked down, suffering severe head injuries. He was taken to Tongren Hospital by police car number 1953, but died at around 6:00 PM after treatment proved ineffective. The body was transferred to the coroner's office for examination. It is said that his son runs the Tongxinglou teahouse in Tilanqiao and has some savings.

Shen Yunjie's Funeral Tomorrow

The Entire Special Police Force Escorts the Coffin

The Municipal Council Will Also Send Detectives to Participate

Mr. Shen Yunjie, a trainee member of the Special Police Force of the Municipal Council, unfortunately died from a gunshot wound due to mistaken identity during a detective's pursuit of thieves. The funeral is scheduled for tomorrow (the 17th) at 2:00 PM. Repairing Jiangxi Road Bridge

Vehicles Temporarily Prohibited

The water bridge on Jiangxi Road was repeatedly hit by barges due to strong winds and high tides on Wednesday and Thursday, causing the pillars to loosen and the bridge to be damaged. The Municipal Council began repairs yesterday, temporarily suspending vehicle traffic. However, ships can still pass unhindered. It is reported that the bridge is a wooden structure and will soon be rebuilt as a large concrete bridge.

Fangcao Bookstore Fined 100 Gold

Prosecuted for Publishing the Book "Degeneracy"

Fangcao Bookstore at 60 Fuzhou Road was prosecuted for publishing the book "Degeneracy".

Page 16

The Police Department's Political Section purchased the book and, after careful reading, found that pages 53, 99, 113, and 117 contained obscene content. Lawyer Qian Xunjiu represented the prosecution, while the bookstore manager Huang Zhong hired a lawyer for defense. Yesterday morning, Judge Luo Renji heard the case. Lawyer Qian first presented the book as evidence and explained the circumstances. Then, the defendant's lawyer listed examples of both old and new novels that involved romance, and argued eloquently. In the end, the judge found the defendant Huang Zhong guilty of distributing publications that harmed good morals and sentenced him to a fine of one hundred yuan. If the fine is not paid, he would be imprisoned for one day for every two yuan. One copy of "Degeneracy" was confiscated.

Preliminary Hearing in the Woman's Strangulation Case

Xu Lu, a woman who lived in front of the Minli Middle School on Zhonghua Road, was strangled to death on the night of March 12th this year. The local court detained the suspects Qiao Fusheng and Ling Xingen. Prosecutor Wu paid close attention to the case and conducted a thorough investigation. In addition to numerous detailed investigations, yesterday he summoned Qiao Fusheng's maid, A Lin, Chen Taohan, Tao, Zhou Qiantai, Wu Xigui, and the deceased's ten-year-old daughter Da Xin and eight-year-old son Jinglu, to the preliminary hearing. It was reported that A Lin stated that she lived next to the escalator, and Qiao Fusheng had to pass her door when he went out. Zhou Qiantai stated that he lived downstairs, and anyone who walked past would have to pass this way. Chen Tao Tao claimed that he slept on a cot at the front door, and anyone entering or leaving at night would have to be opened by him. The official asked if Qiao had gone out on March 12, which was the 23rd night of the first lunar month. They all said that he did not go out. The official then asked the ten-year-old girl and eight-year-old boy, who slept with their mother, if they knew who had harmed their mother. They answered that they were asleep and did not know. Therefore, it is still difficult to identify the murderer. The official ordered them to be dismissed and to wait for further investigation.

Dispute Over the Disappearance of the Village Girl Lianlian

Wang Wenlan Has Major Suspicions

Chen Guangfu, a 55-year-old man from Tongzhou, has been working as a farmer in his hometown. He has a daughter named Lianlian, who is now 19 years old. Since childhood, she has been betrothed to the son of Ji Hejun, a fellow villager, but she has not yet married. Unexpectedly, Lianlian suddenly disappeared on the 15th day of the third lunar month this year. After searching everywhere without success, it was discovered that she was abducted to Shanghai by Wang Yun, a fellow villager. Chen, along with his future father-in-law Ji Hejun, came to Shanghai by boat during the past week and stayed at 7 Yong'an Lane, Yong'an Street, in the French Concession, at the residence of Ji Xichang (Ji's nephew). Every day they went out to inquire about Lianlian's whereabouts, but without any news. A few days ago, a man named Wang Wenlan, also from Tongzhou, contacted Chen. Wang claimed to be familiar with Shanghai and offered to help find her, assuring them that he was confident. However, he first asked for six yuan for travel expenses. Chen readily agreed and paid the money. Unexpectedly, for several days in a row, there was still no sign of Lianlian. Chen then realized he had been fooled. Yesterday, he twisted Wang Wenlan over to the police in Lujiazhai, Pudong, who took him to the third district of the Public Security Bureau. Chen explained the circumstances of his daughter's elopement. Wang Wenlan confessed that he was 24 years old, lived in Wufu Road, Lujiazhai, Pudong, and was engaged in a small business. Because he had a fellow villager relationship with Chen Guangfu and Ji Hejun, they entrusted him to help find Lianlian, and they did give him six yuan for travel expenses. However, the money was stolen by a pickpocket on the way. The district chief questioned him about whether he knew the whereabouts of Chen's daughter. He was vague. Chen Guangfu further stated that the abductor, Wang Yun, was Wang Wenlan's uncle and that he had a strong suspicion of helping to abduct her. As the case was related to a criminal matter, in the afternoon it was judged to transfer the group to the local court for disposal.

A Large Batch of Smuggled Salt Seized

A Large Bamboo Mat Boat

Containing More Than 300 Bags of Salt

Yu Qiutang, captain of the first brigade of the Wusong Su Wu Salt Smuggling Enforcement Team, together with Xu Wenyou, patrol captain of the second brigade, and others, led their officers and men on patrol boats in the outer waters of Chuansha at about 7:30 AM the day before yesterday. They spotted a bamboo mat boat parked at the Beigang Estuary. The captains suspected the boat and went forward to search it. Unexpectedly, as they approached the boat, two people jumped ashore and fled west. They detained the boat and seized a large batch of smuggled salt in the cabin, totaling more than 300 bags. After being informed, captains Li and Xie reported to Director Song of the General Bureau yesterday and removed the smuggled salt from the boat and sent it to Chuansha Salt Depot for temporary storage, pending further action.

Chinese Detective Involved in Morphine Robbery Case on Kele Road - Continued Hearing

Liang Chengyu, a Chinese detective of the Public Concession General Patrol Room, was recently accused by the police of stealing a large amount of morphine. On the morning of the 6th of this month, Western Inspector Yao Ke, General Detective Lu Liankui, and Detective Liu Shaokui of the Inspectorate escorted Liang to the Second Criminal Court of the Special District Local Court for trial. The facts of the accusation were that at 7:00 AM on the 28th of last month, seven robbers suddenly came to a company at 1 Wende Lane, Kele Road, in the French Concession, and robbed morphine worth 50,000 yuan. The stolen goods were later brought into the Public Concession and first placed on Dagu Road, then moved to Danshui Road, and finally hidden in the home of Li Liansheng at 439 Laomale Lane, Chongqing Road. Li was one of the seven robbers who robbed on Kele Road. That evening at 11:00 PM, six bandits came to Li Liansheng's house and robbed all the morphine. Liang Chengyu, a Chinese detective, was accused of being one of the six thieves. After the police arrested Liang, they had Li Liansheng and his concubine identify him as one of the robbers, which was confirmed. This was detailed in the newspaper on the 7th of this month. Yesterday afternoon, it was time for the continued hearing of the case. The defendant's lawyers Ye Fukang, Yuan Yang'an, and others also appeared in court. The police lawyer Zhang Tianyin rose and stated that the case was of great importance and complex. Many people were present in the courtroom, which may slightly hinder the trial. Therefore, he requested to prohibit the audience. Judge Ge Zhiqin approved the request, so all people who were not related to the case were ordered to leave the courtroom. Lawyer Zhang then continued that the police had conducted a detailed investigation during the adjournment and learned that after Li Liansheng and others robbed the morphine from Kele Road, they first hid it at 562 Dagu Road, from 7:10 AM to 7:30 AM, and then moved it to the building at 1500 Hexing Lane, Edward Road. The house was rented by Zhou Fangting. At 9:30 AM, they moved it to 382.5 Defu Lane, Mahuo Road, until 5:00 PM, when they moved it to Male Lane, Chongqing Road. It was robbed that night. Now Dong Lanting and others have been arrested. Please question them. Dong Lanting testified that he was from Ningbo and lived at 7 Fudeli, Edward Road. He was friends with Liang Chengyu. He often came to my house to play. Before May 1st, one evening, Liang received a telegram from Shandong that his father had passed away. He came to my place and said that he wanted to ask for leave to return home. The next evening at 9:00 PM, he talked with Liang at Yao Jinlong's place at 349 Shengping Lane in the French Concession for about two or three hours before they parted ways. The witness Zhou Qu testified that on the afternoon of April 28th, Li Liansheng and his wife came to Male Lane to rent the remaining parlor room in my house. They stated that the monthly rent was 18 yuan. They moved in soon after. In the evening, four people entered through the back door and went straight into the parlor room, claiming to visit Li Liansheng. They did not leave late at night. The next day, I told Li Liansheng that I was terminating the lease. I don't know anything else. The witnesses, women Yang Dai and Zhang Kong, and others also complained. The defendant Liang Chengyu was questioned and still insisted that he did not commit the morphine robbery, and claimed that on that night, he and Dong Lanting went to the French Concession to investigate the party member Xiao Jiang, Wang Zilian and Fang Liansheng, of the Li Huiqing kidnapping case, who was Li Liansheng. Judge Ge verified the testimonies and ordered the defendant to be returned to custody and to wait for the continued hearing on the afternoon of May 26th.

Incoming Mail

Letter from Fan Fayuan et al. to Hu Shuhua

Fan Fayuan et al. wrote to Hu Shuhua, the Shanghai representative to the National Assembly, regarding traditional Chinese medicine: "Mr. Shuhua, greetings. We rushed to the capital a few days ago, intending to unite with colleagues to hold a meeting to welcome you upon your arrival in Beijing, to express our long-standing intentions. Upon hearing that you had already traveled north, we were only able to promote your return to Shanghai due to business constraints and urgent telegrams. We were unable to achieve our purpose and regret it to this day. Recently, we read in the Shanghai Shen Xin newspapers in the local news column an article that the Shanghai Medical Association petitioned you to submit a proposal to the National Assembly. The general idea is: (1) Please ask the government to establish Western medical schools and hospitals everywhere, and designate Western medicine as the national medicine of the Republic of China. (2) Falsely accuse traditional Chinese medicine of violating science, limit traditional Chinese medicine to a one-time registration, so that no more traditional Chinese medicine practitioners will be allowed to be produced in the future. (3) To organize and manage traditional Chinese medicine with Western medicine, and so on, and only send Pang Jingzhou as a representative to go to Beijing to negotiate. Although on the surface it claims to be for the country and the people, its purpose is to eliminate our country's inherent medicine. Colleagues in both the traditional Chinese medicine and traditional Chinese medicine industries have been running around alarmed, and the public is indignant. If such a proposal is unfortunately passed, I am afraid that not only will traditional Chinese medicine and traditional Chinese medicine go bankrupt from now on, but the loss to the country will also be unbearable. Now the relationship between interests and harms is briefly stated separately below, and I hope that you will be informed. (1) Establishing Western medical schools and hospitals everywhere is not only beyond the financial resources of the country recently, but also the gains are not worth the losses. Why do we say this? All the instruments and medicines used by Western medicine now need to be supplied from foreign countries. Some say that 'Western medicine in China is like a foreign medicine salesperson disguised as a mailman.' Considering the actual situation, it is not an exaggeration. Establishing one more Western medical school will cultivate several more 'foreign drug salesmen.' Shouldn't Western medicine practitioners with a little patriotism do their best to promote the imitation and manufacture of foreign medicines and machinery? Is it true that scientists do not need to consider the national economy? The national economy is the lifeblood of the country. Every penny that flows out means a loss of the national lifeblood. According to the current Chinese medicine, there are no more than 10,000 people, and the annual import of foreign drugs has reached more than 200 million yuan. A little consideration is enough to shock people. If we vigorously promote Western medical schools and hospitals all over the country before we can produce Western medicine in our country, even if traditional Chinese medicine cannot cure a single disease, even if Western medicine is truly omnipotent and cures all diseases, I am afraid that the people's diseases will be cured, and the country's lifeblood will be cut off. Is it like scientific principles to seek for the people but not for the country? As for asking to designate Western medicine as the Chinese national medicine, it is even more nonsense. According to the association's previous article opposing the central government's establishment of a 'National Medical Center' to lead the organization of traditional Chinese medicine, it said, (Medicine is the common property of the world, and academic studies should not have national boundaries,) and then said, (Before traditional Chinese medicine has been organized and completed to become an independent oriental medicine, it should not be called national medicine,) 'extracting the original meaning,' etc. Not long ago, unexpectedly, in the blink of an eye, they were willing to give up the names of new medicine practitioners and ask to call themselves national medicine practitioners. Is it because their medical knowledge knows that it cannot be shared with the world, and can only be called national medicine? Or has Chinese medicine in China recently become an independent oriental medicine? Its contradiction and ridiculousness are truly difficult to understand. According to the members of the association, some graduated from domestic schools, and some studied in England, America, Germany, France, and Japan. Should we call the former Chinese medicine practitioners, or the latter Chinese medicine practitioners, or both Chinese medicine practitioners? The lectures are all in foreign languages, and the supplies are all foreign goods. To call this 'national' is like calling imported goods domestic goods, and Western clothes national clothes, which is no different from robbing others of their beauty and making the world laugh. And since there is Chinese medicine, there cannot be Chinese medicine. Since Western medicine is Chinese medicine, is Western medicine Chinese medicine? Those who boast of being new medicine and call themselves scientists, have this kind of view, so it is no wonder that old medicine does not know science. (2) Science cannot be separated from facts, and separation from facts is not science. The main purpose of medicine is to cure diseases. Whether traditional Chinese medicine can cure diseases, whether its curative effect is inferior to Western medicine, and whether traditional Chinese medicine has a necessity and possibility to be limited, sensible people will have a fair opinion. Only arguing for the name of science without arguing for the fact of curing diseases is already a dispute that violates science. Moreover, Western medicine is Western medicine, Chinese medicine is Chinese medicine, each treats its own affairs, and there is no mutual obstruction at first. Chinese medicine is not an obstacle to Western medicine. Why does Western medicine deliberately want Chinese medicine to be destroyed and then quickly? Whether this kind of expression is in line with science is not discussed for the time being. Whether a Western medicine professional group publicly requests the elimination of Chinese medicine exceeds the scope and has ulterior motives, everyone knows. The traditional Chinese medicine community will not bother to argue with it about academic theories. The reason why Japan does not value traditional Chinese medicine is that traditional Chinese medicine in Japan, like Western medicine, is imported from Japan. Moreover, it was easy to send people to learn Western medicine at that time, but it was difficult to send people to master Chinese medicine. It is also not difficult to manufacture artificial Western medicine, but it is not easy to produce natural Chinese medicine. For the sake of the people, both Western medicine and traditional Chinese medicine are acceptable. For the sake of the country, we have to limit the imperial Chinese medicine. The Chinese medicine of our country is our own, and the agriculture, industry, and commerce of Chinese medicine are in the tens of millions. The situation is exactly the opposite. How can we cite it as an example? Moreover, Japan's crackdown on Chinese medicine was still decades ago. What is the situation of Chinese medicine today? Both the upper and lower levels are trying to revitalize it, and the parliament is also on the agenda. Why does the association only know what is far away and not what is near, or know what is near and deliberately abandon it? In short, the theory of limiting Chinese medicine to a one-time registration is enough to put the Republic of China in a state of economic downturn. It is truly a heresy that is not in line with national conditions, hinders people's livelihood, and violates scientific principles. (3) The academic theories of Chinese medicine and Western medicine are different. Organizing Chinese medicine with Western medicine is like using a coachman as a construction engineer. The result must be the opposite of the purpose and is unimaginable. Chinese medicine theories are mostly formed after experience. Chinese medicine theories must be organized. Chinese medicine experience will never die. The strength of Chinese medicine lies in having another experience. The weakness of Chinese medicine lies in the inconsistency between the theory and experience. Therefore, if you want to organize Chinese medicine, you must use its experience as a tool for organization, and you must never use Western medicine theory as a standard for organization, because the starting points are completely different. Looking around at Chinese medicine in our country, there are few who have Chinese medicine theories, and even fewer who have Chinese medicine experience. If Western medicine practitioners who have no experience in Chinese medicine are responsible for organizing Chinese medicine, does it mean using their Chinese medicine theories to organize it? Chinese medicine will never be successful. Does it mean using their Western medicine knowledge to organize Chinese medicine? If you do not completely change Chinese medicine into Western medicine, you will lead Chinese medicine to a path that is neither donkey nor horse. Losing the true face of Chinese medicine and destroying the true value of Chinese medicine is the same. Moreover, there is even more progress. In this proposal of the association, first, it said that old medicine uses unscientific bases, performs incomplete methods, and advocates abandonment, which is reasonable.... Then, it said that scientific medical experts should be hired to study old medicine, so that they can organize old medical techniques, hoping to eliminate the false and preserve the true, and preserve the national heritage.... According to the former statement, old medicine is useless, and abandoning it is not a pity. According to the latter statement, old medicine still has true things that can be preserved and the value of national heritage. The inconsistency between the former and latter is so serious that a scientist dares to send this contradictory statement to the sacred and solemn National Assembly. What is their intention? What is their value? Clear and wise as you, sir, will definitely be able to see through their bottom line and see through their treachery. The essence of medicine for more than 4,000 years, and the three million traditional Chinese medicine and commercial workers, the survival and destruction are not only related to the people's livelihood, but also related to the nation. I hope that you, sir, will use your usual aspirations for love to lend a hand in this critical moment, and find a way to dispel the above-mentioned proposals by the Shanghai Medical Association that are harmful to the national economy and the people's livelihood, and refuse to submit them. I respectfully ask all traditional Chinese medicine colleagues across the country to bow their heads and make a request. I hope that you will give us guidance at any time. This is the honor and good fortune. Sincerely, Fan Fayuan, Gu Weichuan, Cai Jiping, Shen Zhuoru, Cheng Diren, Xu Xiangren, and others."

Free Talk

A Word of Insight

— Yao Cheng

The sage Cangjie created the word "情" (emotion/feeling), constructing it from a passionate heart. However, in modern human relationships, the word "情" has lost its precious heart.

Love for gold is the most popular form of social interaction in the current era of marriage.

Crying is the subject of laughter. Only a woman's tears are worthless. Likewise, only a woman's smile is worth a thousand gold pieces.

Most of the women who sell smiles in brothels are not accustomed to living a life of hardship.

The first sound an infant makes upon entering the world is a cry, seemingly knowing in advance that there is more sorrow than joy in the world. It seems that all living beings come to repay a debt of tears.

Men who indulge in brothels and are intoxicated and unaware are probably echoing Bao Yu's saying, "Men are made of mud, and women are made of water."

The ratio of virtuous mothers and good wives to those who file for divorce in court and request alimony is one to nine.

A writer's pen is like a soldier's gun. Losing a pen is like a soldier being disarmed. Both cannot survive.

Record of the Words and Deeds of Zhao Guantao's Respected Father

— Sun Choucheng

Zhao Guantao, the current commander of the Sixth Division of the Army stationed in Xinyang, Henan, is a native of Sheng County, Zhejiang. His home is located in Taoyuan Township, at the foot of Mount Duxiu, and he is from the same hometown as Wang Xiaolai, the chairman of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce. The two families are only a few miles apart, so Mr. Wang knows his family history very well. According to him, Commander Zhao's respected father, Mr. Shi Gao, is highly regarded in his hometown. His words and deeds throughout his life are sufficient as a model for future generations. Therefore, I have extracted a few examples to substantiate this discussion.

Mr. Zhao's given name was Hongxiang, and his courtesy name was Shi Gao. He was born when the Taiping Rebellion began. His father and elder brother were captured, and his mother also passed away early. He was raised by his uncle. At the age of nine, he entered a private school and studied several hundred words of Confucian classics daily. Due to poverty and famine, he could not afford the tuition. He went out to tend cattle. As he grew older, he possessed great strength and was skilled in riding and archery. He took the county examination and entered the military academy as the top candidate. He once took the provincial examination, but his horse stumbled, and he failed the examination. He then gave up all intention of seeking advancement. When the local bandits, led by Wu Dai, caused turmoil, threatening the city, the county magistrate was unable to help. The local gentry gathered for discussions day and night, but could not come up with a solution. Mr. Zhao requested strict defense and personally went to the provincial capital to request reinforcements. He presented his case to the authorities, who then dispatched troops. He made decisive plans and did not sleep day or night. After more than a month, they achieved a great victory, beheading the bandit leader. After the matter was settled, the prefect admired his talent and wanted to offer him an official position, but he refused. He was resolute and decisive by nature, and his uprightness was sufficient to convince people. Whenever there were discussions on public welfare in the city and countryside, and opinions were divided, he would often settle the matter with a few words. The local people were originally strong and fond of litigation, but from then on, they all sought Mr. Zhao's judgment. For decades, they did not bring lawsuits to the magistrate. Between the years of Renyin and Guimao, obscene songs and plays became prevalent. Mr. Zhao abhorred them and prohibited them from entering the area. He kept watch to prevent them from entering. Some unscrupulous fellows brought in lewd actors, gathering crowds to sing and dance. Mr. Zhao returned home suddenly. The actors, in their makeup and costumes, and the audience all scattered. Mr. Zhao had a tall and imposing appearance, with a beautiful beard. He wore simple, clean clothing, and his eyes shone like lightning. Although his family was poor, he was very generous. An old woman in the neighborhood and her son relied on farming rented land for a living. In a year of famine, the landlord demanded rent urgently. The mother and son clung to each other and wept. Mr. Zhao shared grain with them. When the old woman died without the means to pay for a coffin, he provided the coffin and burial clothes. He enjoyed having guests. Regretting his lack of education, he was especially respectful to scholars. He had three sons. The eldest, Xueyong, and the youngest, Xuezhen, served as captains of the Sheng County patrol team successively. The second son was Commander Guantao. He trained and supervised them strictly, teaching them in the morning and examining their actions in the evening. He always warned them to be diligent and hardworking. He once said, "The only thing our ancestors left behind is this word 'hardship.' Hardship is our family's business. If we are content and enjoy ourselves, will we not fall into ruin?" When the Xinhai Revolution broke out, the martyr Chen Ying士 was about to lead the Northern Expedition. Guantao abandoned his studies and secretly enlisted in the army. His father and elder brother discussed pursuing him to bring him back, but Mr. Zhao refused. He laughed and said, "I am old. If I were young and strong, I would have raced ahead of my sons!" When Guantao went on the expedition to Shandong and Hebei, he said, "You went without telling me, and I do not blame you. But if you encounter hardship and return out of fear, then that is what I will greatly despise." Sheng Mountain is a mountainous area, and therefore has many bandits. Between the years of Xinhai and Renzi, the bandits became even more rampant. Mr. Zhao established a local militia and led them in defense, just as he had done in suppressing Wu Dai's bandit rebellion. As a result, the village was free from trouble. For sixteen years, he persisted without懈怠. The bandits were unable to succeed. In his later years, he loved the scenery of Mount Duxiu. The mountain sits on the upper reaches of the 剡溪 River, overlooking a vast plain, with the beauty of secluded springs and strange rocks. There are relics of Zhang Sheng, Lady Wei, and Wang Youjun. He often rode his horse among them, caressing every bridge and every stone. When he was critically ill, Xueyong was about to summon Guantao to return. Mr. Zhao angrily rebuked him, saying, "What do I expect of your younger brother? Do I want him to be reluctant to say goodbye? The founding of the Party-state and the initial pacification of Jiangnan, and the long drive to expel the north, is precisely the day of your family's destruction! Your younger brother has long cherished the ambition of revolution, but his wish has not been fulfilled. Now, taking advantage of the momentum of victory, he charges into battle. How can there not be someone like 狼瞫 to assist him? What regrets do I have?" He passed away on March 15th of the sixteenth year of the Republic, at the age of seventy-five. The villagers still praise Mr. Zhao's virtues to this day. Commander Guantao, at that time, was deeply involved in military affairs and was serving far away, enduring hardship as a soldier. Having failed to serve his parents, he suffered grief and regret. Almost five years have passed. Now that military affairs have become slightly less pressing, he plans to widely solicit writings in order to leave a model for future generations.

Plum Catkins of Luofu

— Fei

One day after Mei Lanfang arrived in Guangzhou, the Guangzhou theater community held a grand welcome meeting at the Renhe Guild Hall. Many nearby residents flocked to see Mr. Mei's elegant demeanor. The temporary gathering numbered tens of thousands of people, and the roads were blocked. Some people started disputes due to the crowds and inability to get in. Fortunately, the military police maintained order, preventing any accidents. The warm welcome the Cantonese people gave to Mei Lanfang is evident from this.

Since the performances began in Guangzhou, there has not been a single day without a full house. The daily income is always over eight thousand yuan. Although rumors have recently proliferated, ticket sales remain as strong as ever. It is as if the saying "Who cares about the rise and fall of the nation, the whole city is talking about 呌天儿" is being lived out.

Ouyang Yuqian established a drama research institute in Guangdong, which has been quite successful. Mr. Mei made a special visit. The old friends were delighted to meet again. The next day, Ouyang hosted a banquet for Mr. Mei. During the dinner, there was a detailed discussion on the reform of drama. Ouyang said that old operas have many strengths, but they must adapt to modern trends and gradually improve. Mr. Mei deeply agreed with this and recounted his experiences after visiting America. He spoke eloquently for hours. The two friends were very congenial.

Mr. Mei performed at the Haizhu Theater for a week and went to Hong Kong on May 6. He was scheduled to perform at the Ko Shing Theatre on the 7th and until the 11th. On the 12th, he returned to Guangzhou to continue performing for another eleven days, which will be the end of the run.

After Mr. Mei's performances in Guangdong, he may travel to Southeast Asia. Negotiations are currently underway. If this becomes a reality, he will definitely return to Shanghai after Guangdong before going there. This is because the completion ceremony of Mr. Du Yuesheng's family ancestral hall will be held on April 25th of the lunar calendar, and Mr. Mei has already made an appointment to perform for the celebration.

Dragon Boat Race on a New Dragon Boat Festival

— Rui Hongchu

Morley Town is densely populated, with many shops and thriving businesses. There are a total of 30 schools for boys and girls, all well-organized. The fifth day of the fifth month of the Gregorian calendar is the traditional Dragon Boat Festival. Each school traditionally takes a day off to celebrate. Two days prior, Ms. Jin Wenjun, the principal of the Xiuming Girls' School, initiated a dragon boat race as a form of exercise. Two hundred boys and girls signed up. They first took a boat to test their paddling skills, and thirty people were selected. Thirty small boats were hired. The boats' bows and sterns were decorated with paper dragons, baring their teeth and claws. Small electric light bulbs were installed in their eyes. At eight o'clock in the morning of that day, a dragon boat race was held on the canal. Prominent figures from all walks of life and principals of boys' and girls' schools were present to watch with pleasure. Ms. Jin ordered the students to board the boats, one person per boat. A small flag was inserted on each dragon's head, fluttering in the wind. Mr. Xu Mengyi, the principal of Morley School, served as the judge and issued the order to start. The paddles went down in unison, and the boats shot forward, splashing water everywhere. In the end, Shi Fangmao, a student from the Sericulture School, won the championship and was awarded a painting of an ink dragon. Applause thundered. After the race, the students disembarked and dispersed, singing the dragon boat race song.

"Rejection" in Dream of the Red Chamber

— Romantic Scholar

The book Dream of the Red Chamber has captivated countless young men and women. The merit of this book lies not only in its profound depiction of emotions but also in its vivid portrayal of events. Taking Wang Xifeng's way of handling affairs as an example, the item of "rejection" in Dream of the Red Chamber can be roughly divided into three types.

(1) Rejecting his return.

(2) Not good at rejecting his return.

(3) Not good at rejecting.

The first type is what Fengjie is accustomed to using against those maids and servants. Because these maids and servants have nothing to rely on in the Rongguo Mansion, she straightforwardly and happily "rejects" them when they do something wrong. The second type is what Fengjie uses against Bao Yu, Dai Yu, Xi Chun, Bao Chai, and others. Because although they themselves have no power, they are all deeply loved by the Old Matriarch, so whenever something happens, she often "is not good at rejecting their return." She can only use some methods to deal with them, or give them a 70% or 80% discount, using a compromise to resolve the matter. The third type is what Fengjie uses against the Old Matriarch, Madam Wang, Aunt Xue, and others. Because these are simply the direct superiors, she obeys them in everything, and "is not good at rejecting." Besides following orders carefully, what other way is there?

After reading the above situation, we can't help but draw a small analogy to the big. From the way things are handled in a family, we are reminded of the current government offices. Nowadays, many intermediate agencies deal with political affairs, and are probably no different from this situation. When dealing with ordinary people, they may handle things impartially, and "reject their return" for things that are not right. When dealing with people who have some reputation, then, for the sake of face, they are not good at directly rejecting their return. They can only think of a way to give them a compromise mediation. If they encounter a big shot or their own superior, then it is really "not good at rejecting." Besides obeying orders, what other way is there?

Around the Yellow Sea (4)

— Huang Yanpei

Rotary Club Speaking Department

Hawthorne Case Conversion (15)

— Cheng Xiaoqing

Hawthorne suddenly raised his head and looked at me and asked, "What does his face look like?" I replied, "His face is long and his chin is slightly pointed." Hawthorne's eyes suddenly flashed. As if he had gotten some clue, he pressed on and asked, "Is there anything special about his face? Did you notice it too?" I was very proud to hear this question and replied, "This time I am confident that my vision has not been negligent. I think there are two obvious differences on that person's face: first, his eyes are somewhat angular —" At this moment, Hawthorne suddenly exclaimed, "Ha! That second different point isn't the tip of his nose a bit hooked?" If I hadn't been sitting in the car at this time, I would have jumped up. I couldn't help but clap my hands and cheered, "That's right. You saw him too?" Hawthorne did not answer and then asked, "Isn't his bow tie white with tiny blue stars?" I hesitated for a moment and replied, "Probably, but I didn't pay much attention." Hawthorne also said. "The whiteness on his face is mostly the result of snow cream. Isn't it?" I nodded again. "Exactly. Exactly." Hawthorne said. "There is also a strong fragrance nearby." I hurriedly replied, "Yes, yes. That can't be wrong——" Hawthorne then hurriedly interrupted and said, "His hair that has been smeared with Stancome is combed flat back——Oh. I was wrong. You can't see this." I couldn't help but raise my right palm. Pat him on the shoulder. I shouted, "Enough. Enough. There will never be any mistakes again. Do you know this person?" Our conversation was at a tense moment. My body shook. The car had already stopped. I poked my head out and took a look. This is already Lin Yin Road. The car is parked in front of my residence. I got out of the car. Then I invited Hawthorne to sit in my residence for a while. I was still enthusiastically inviting guests at this time. I can't deny that all I wanted to do was to end my question. Hawthorne suddenly declined. "I'm sorry. I can't obey. I should have gone in to ask about your wife's illness. But it's late at night. I'll come to ask tomorrow." So before I parted with him. I had to re-propose my last question. Hawthorne shook his head and said, "I don't know him. But when I was in the Gao family. My eyes were not as focused as yours. I have indeed seen him. But it's not of much use in reality. What I mean. If we want to investigate the whereabouts of this person. We might as well start with your aunt-in-law. You can only take on this move. If there is any clue. Let's discuss the second step of the implementation method."

Silk and Tea: The Current Situation of Changxing Spring Silkworms is Terrible

Purely Damaged by Cold Rain

This year's spring silkworm feeding amount in Changxing's various markets and villages is still not weak, but the early silkworms suffered from cold weather and reduced egg hatching. The climate was unusually cold after the late silkworms started to sleep, coupled with little sunshine and much rain. The silkworms' development was unfavorable. The early silkworms are now opening leaves after the first sleep. Due to continuous heavy rain, many silkworms are suffering from white muscardine disease. The late silkworms are also in their third sleep and have started consuming leaves. Due to eating wet leaves, yellowing has been observed. The current situation is terrible.

European and American Factory Jing Silk: Telegraphic Transfer Prices Still Small

Yesterday, the Shanghai foreign trading house yarn market still tended to be peaceful. It was found that the overseas market's daily silk opening prices were increasingly lower, and the telegraphic transfer prices for Shanghai white factory Jing silk were increasingly smaller. Chinese merchants found it difficult to sell their heavy loads. Yesterday, only Weicheng and others took 20 bales of Shanghai white factory Jing silk, and Xinfu took 40 bales of Baiqian Jing silk. The prices remained stable.

The Stunning Debut of Qihong's New Crop

The Qimen new black tea, which has attracted attention from both Chinese and foreigners, arrived yesterday by the Yangtze River with more than 2,900 boxes. Including the previous batches, there are more than 3,000 boxes on the market. Due to the excellent aroma of the tea leaves, it has attracted great attention from the British. The market atmosphere is unusually tense. Initially, Baochang & Co. opened with 280 taels for the top lot. Jardine, Concord, Jinlong, and other firms expressed their eagerness and rushed to bid. Depending on the quality of the goods, the bidding continued to reach beyond 300 taels. Finally, the Liulv brand sold by Yuanfengrun Tea House opened at the top price of 360 taels. This high price is unprecedented in history. This year, the Qimen estates focused on harvesting green leaves early, resulting in excellent products and developed European sales, which fully demonstrates that China's tea foreign trade urgently needs fundamental improvement as soon as possible.

Jiangxi Province's Tea Season

Wuning black tea has always been famous. In recent years, due to foreign merchants suppressing prices, most tea businesses have suffered losses and have been unable to pay high prices for purchases. Mountain households have also reduced planting due to low prices, leading to a sharp decline in the natural quality product. This year, the Tea Industry Association paid attention to improvements, widely issued declarations, and persuaded mountain households to open gardens early and process and manufacture. Tea shops also offered high prices and limited the harvest to before Grain Rain and the end of weighing to before the Beginning of Summer. Now, all the goods from each estate have been collected, with estimated costs averaging 60 to 70 taels, more than double the previous year. However, the gardens opened earlier this year, and the goods are extremely tender. The weather is sunny and the aroma is especially good. In the future, when transported to Shanghai, high prices are expected. This year's turnaround is truly due to the efforts of the Tea Industry Association's promotion.

More Than Ten New Local Tea Factories Added

Due to sluggish business in recent years, the number of local tea factories in Shanghai has decreased from more than 80 to more than 30. When the new tea came on the market this year, most tea factories adopted a wait-and-see attitude, and purchases were sparse. However, since the opening of the new tea market, tea merchants have seized the opportunity to reorganize and sent personnel to the mountains to purchase. According to recent surveys, there are already 46 tea factories in Shanghai, an increase of more than ten from before.

Tunxi Tea Firms are Launching Scales

The early new tea from Xiuyi County has already been harvested and the gardens are closed. The famous high-grade estate teas will also be half-harvested. The tea firms in Tunxi's Liyang and Shuikou areas have seen the Shanghai market's stock of Zhenmei tea being low, and the sales of Xiumei, Zhenmei, and lower-grade teas to France becoming smooth, so their interest has greatly increased. Recently, many tea firms have launched scales, specializing in searching for the leading teas before the Beginning of Summer in the northeast of Wu and the southeast of Xiuyi, hoping to obtain more genuine goods and increase sales prices. The Tunpu money shops have transported large amounts of silver from Shanghai and Hangzhou to meet the needs of the tea firms due to the new tea coming on the market and the urgent need for funds. Recently, Shanghai notes have been selling for 1,380 yuan to 1,376 yuan per thousand, and the money supply has become active, with the tea market showing signs of gradually becoming lively.

Wuyi Tea Affected by Heavy Rain

Since the opening of the gardens for the new tea in Wuyi County, the weather has been overcast and rainy. Recently, there have been heavy downpours and mountain floods. The tea-picking men and women have been working hard in the mud and water every day. The tea leaves are soaked in rain, stiff and not soft, and grow very quickly, easily becoming old and grassy. In the beginning, many households with more tea reduced the number of workers hired to save money, as they thought the mountain prices would be difficult to increase this year. Unexpectedly, the weather was unfavorable, and they were all struggling to harvest and process in time. Today, all families are adding extra female tea workers, braving the rain to pick and intensify the roasting, as the tea is growing rapidly and cannot be delayed. According to this, the cost of picking workers and firewood is more than double the old cost. The cost for small households has increased compared to last year, and the tea production is again suffering losses. Therefore, under the tea trees in the tea gardens, one can hear the complaints and sighs of these people everywhere.

Sugar Market: Raw Brown Sugar Opens with More Than 4,000 Bags

Yesterday, the sugar market received telegrams from the producing areas: Cuban current sugar prices remained unchanged, New York sugar futures for May remained unchanged, and the other months fell back by 1 point each. Java current and futures sugar also had no fluctuations. The market's negotiated transactions were quite active. Dutch No. 24 coarse sand white sugar rose to 10 taels 05 qian and a half, and high-quality goods rose to 10 taels 07 qian, with more than 1,000 bags being transacted. This was an increase of 5 fen compared to the previous day, and the market sentiment was strong. No. 20 medium sand sugar was priced at 10 taels 01 qian and a half, with little demand. The daily market was active, and the market price gradually trended upwards. N Mark was priced at 10 taels 06 qian and 2.5 fen to 6 qian and a half, TK Mark was priced at 10 taels 06 qian, and later shouted for 10 taels 07 qian, TX Mark was priced at 10 taels 09 qian, YP Mark was priced at 10 taels 09 qian and a half, TM Mark was priced at 10 taels 03 qian, J Mark was priced at 11 taels to 11 taels 05 fen, YT Mark was priced at 10 taels 05 qian and a half, YRO Mark was priced at 9 taels 9 qian 7.5 fen, and Minghua goods were priced at 10 taels. The market was generally brisk and showed signs of further increase. For the sale of spot goods for May and June, Wanqing Bingchang & Co. sold 200 tons at a silver price of 8 taels 1 qian. Huaxin & Co. opened with more than 1,000 bags of spot medium sand white sugar, priced at 10 taels 01 qian. More than 4,000 bags of raw brown sugar were priced at 9 taels 2 qian, which was an increase of 1 qian compared to the previous market. The factory's Binghua Qing sugar, for delivery in three weeks, opened at 9 taels 4 qian and a half. Guohuo Huanggang Qing sugar opened with 400 bags, priced at 7 taels 8 qian and a half to 7 taels 9 qian, and high-quality goods were shouted for 8 taels 2 qian, but there were few buyers at the moment. Wufu Bing sugar opened with 180 boxes, priced at 8 taels 5 qian, a decrease of 2 qian compared to the previous market. The market shape was generally firm and brisk.

Hardware: New Black Iron Nails Arrive

Because there are not many black iron nails on the market, they are also a popular item on the market recently. Various groups, such as those from Tianjin, Yantai, Qingdao, Yingkou, and Andong, are all purchasing them. As a result, the market supply is becoming increasingly scarce, and the standard price has risen by several qian. Currently, a double box of 3-point nails sells for 61 taels 5 qian, a single box sells for 31 taels 4 fen, a double box of 60 taels, and a single box of 30 taels 07 qian and a half. A double box of 5-point nails sells for 59 taels 5 qian, a single box of 30 taels, and a double box of 6-point nails sells for 58 taels, a single box of 30 taels. It is heard that groups from Sichuan, Nanjing, and Wuhu are also sending telegrams to purchase them, but lament that there are no goods to buy. It is heard that new goods, such as 400 to 500 boxes shipped by Xintai Ancient Store yesterday, will surely create a lively scene in the market.

Piece Goods: White Background Colored Tings are Selling Very Well

Yesterday, the piece goods trade was very active due to the warm weather, so summer goods were unusually active. Among them, the white background printed colored Tings were selling the best. Local and domestic merchants were strongly purchasing them, priced from 2 qian 05 li to 2 qian 2 fen and a half. More than 200 pieces were transacted yesterday. Striped Fu silk has already become scarce. The Huxinting Qingguan Mirror is quickly selling out. Arrow Lai Tu is selling for 4 qian 05 li. Yuansubu is still difficult to improve due to the large amount of spot goods. Li Taibai is priced at 14 taels 1 qian, Little Beauty at 12 taels 05 fen, Dian Qiuxiang at 10 taels 03 qian, and Hanshan Temple Double Children Deer at 10 taels 01 qian and a half. White trend cloth is also showing signs of life, but the upper-body goods are quite popular, probably because there are few arrivals. Black goods are not selling as well as before due to the unfavorable season. There was no significant change in Zhigongni yesterday. Although there is a market for fine Biji, the number is also small. Blue striped colored Tings have slightly fallen due to the impact of abundant arrivals. Jun Nong Tu and Yang Guifei have all fallen to 2 qian 2 fen and a half, Kewai Chunfeng to 2 qian 6 fen and 7 li and a half, and Putuoshan to 2 qian 7 fen and 2 li and a half. There is a shortage of spot goods for printed Zhigongni and medium-grade Zhigongduan.
